 ฒฐ ฑฐฑ฿ ฿ฐ ฐฑ฿฿฿฿฿฿ฒ฿ฒ฿฿฿ฒ฿฿ ฿ฑฒฒ ฿ฒ฿฿฿฿฿ ฿ฑ ฒ
 ฒ  ฐ฿ฐฑ฿ฐฑฒ ฿฿ฐ฿฿฿ฐฑฒ ฿ฑฒฐ฿ฐฑฒฐฑ฿ ฒ  ฐฑฒ ฐฑฒฑฒ฿฿
 ฒ  ฐฐฑ  ฐฑ฿ฐฑ฿ฐฑ฿฿ ฐฐฑ ฿ฐฒ฿ ฐฑ ฐ฿ฐฑฐฑ฿ฐฑ฿฿ฐฑ ฐฐฒ
 ฒ ฐฐฐฐ    ฐ ฐ ฐฑ ฐ฿ฐฒฒฐฐ ฐ฿ฐ ฐ ฐฐฑ ฿฿   ฐ  ฐ ฒ
 ฒ ฑฐ ฐ ฒฐฐฑฐฑ฿ ฐฑ฿฿ฒ ฐฒฒ ฐ ฐ฿ฐ ฐฐฑ฿ ฿฿ ฐ ฐฒ
 ฐ ฐฐ ฿฿ฐฐ฿  ฐ ฿ฐฐ฿฿ ฿ ฐ฿ฒ ฐ ฿฿ฐฐ฿฿ฐ฿ ฿ฐ฿ฐฒ
  ฿฿  ฿  ฿   


 ฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿
                                                                             
     Reporter : Hitex/Rebel Chicken       Interviewee : <Undisclosed>        
     Subject  : Piracy Laws               Affiliation : FBI                  
                                                                             
 


 ฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿
                                                                             
       We got the idea for this project a few issues back when we didn't     
   know what to write about for the next issue and were feeling that both    
   of the e-mags were beginning to get a little repetitive, and that we      
   needed to have something new, yet something essential for the warez       
   public to hear of.  While brainstorming, it seeemed that almost on the    
   same note, Rebel Chicken and I jumped and said "Let's interview the       
   FBI!!!"  We giggled a bit, laughed at our apparent stupidity,             
   childishness, and moreover, FOOLISHNESS, and continued to brainstorm.  I  
   don't think we were at all forgetting about this new idea, though, and    
   not five minutes later, we came back to it.                               
                                                                             
       We began to think more rationally, and attempted to find a way of     
   having a close encounter with the Federal Bureau of Investigation         
   without risking our own safety.  We have worked over the period of        
   approximately three weeks to try to get you the best scoop that we        
   could.  We feel that our coverage is very thorough and that we have done  
   an awesome job getting the important facts out, the facts that we should  
   all know if we're going to stay in this business.  We sincerely hope      
   that you will enjoy this section, we have spent many hours working on     
   it, and we are quite sure that you will find it useful and informative.   
                                                                             
 
                                                                             
   Now for some background information:                                      
                                                                             
       Recently a new branch of the FBI opened up near our area, San         
   Francisco, California, USA.  The main reason that this agent knew so      
   much about the topic we were studying is (apart from a bit of luck on     
   our part) that this branch is dedicated to the investigation of computer  
   related crimes.  A bit for my own good, I wanted to investigate this to   
   see if they were coming for me, or for the perverts that hang out on      
   #gaysex and trade GIFs.                                                   
                                                                             
   How us Mofos started this search:                                         
                                                                             
       We started by finding a good, comfortable pay phone, namely one with  
   a nice, soft chair, that we could sit on for the length of an interview   
   and be no less comfortable than we would be if we were sitting our asses  
   in front of IRC :-).  We spotted the perfect one, nice, deserted area,    
   and a soft chair!  We were rather excited, went back home, got the        
   number to the department, a tape recorder (despite the fact that the      
   FBI agent preferred we didn't tape it) and headed back to our site.  We   
   called the office, asked to speak with the press person, and were         
   greeted by a very nice person (as most press-people should be!).  We      
   asked whether or not anybody would be able to grant us a phone interview  
   and just as she was about to decline, she spotted an agent that didn't    
   seem to be doing much.  She transferred us to his line, and the           
   interview began (We got a tad more nervous :-).  Here, read on!!!         
                                                                             
 
                                                                             
                                                                             
    Q  : The FBI (Federal Bureau of Investigation) was first started in an   
         attempt to arrest Al Capone for his bootlegging crimes.  Since the  
         computer age, the government has ushered a new objective for this   
         force.  No longer is the FBI solely responsible for drug dealing    
         and homicides, but they have been granted a greater jurisdiction    
         because it is now responsible for the investigation of other        
         high-tech computer related crimes.  What are your main concerns     
         involving computer crime?                                           
                                                                             
    A  : Computer crime has brought upon us a much more difficult form of    
         crime to investigate.  Currently, our main interests involving      
         computer crime are to eliminate child pornography, credit card      
         fraud, and grand theft.  Such crimes are difficult to investigate   
         because of the distance between the investigator and the suspect,   
         the ease of impersonation, and the Constitution, which keeps us     
         from breaking into high-level programs to grab information about    
         a suspect.  This is still a relatively new field for us, and due    
         to the high rate of development and advancement in technology,      
         our staff's methods must keep up with those of the criminals.       
                                                                             
    Q  : Can you please elaborate on the three main concerns that the FBI    
         department is facing?                                               
                                                                             
    A  : Credit card fraud involves people hacking into the Internet and     
         virtually tapping lines where they grab credit card numbers. Then   
         they use the cards as they would their own, often buying thousands  
         of dollars' worth of goods.  Child pornography has come to an       
         all time high this past year.  Pornography has always been around,  
         but it seems that a new form of it has plagued us.  Explicit        
         photographs of boys and girls as young as 8 years old have been     
         found on the Internet, and the government has not been able to do   
         anything about it due to their limited control of people "freely    
         expressing" themselves.  Grand theft is estimated to have been      
         going on for roughly 15 years, making it one of the oldest          
         computer crimes around.  Grand theft often involves the trading     
         of unlicensed software, severely hurting software distribution      
         companies.                                                          
                                                                             
    Q  : What keeps the government from completely banning child             
         pornography?                                                        
                                                                             
    A  : The United States of America is just that, a set of states, united  
         under one law, the Constitution.  However, the 10th amendment       
         states that all laws not clearly defined within the bill of         
         rights be given to the states.  Thus, different states have quite   
         different laws, including those of child pornography.  Keeping      
         within the laws would be simple for each individual state, but      
         with the Internet, it has become virtually impossible to control    
         data, as most of the time, one does not even know what state s/he   
         is sharing data with.  Even with the passing of laws regulating     
         such activity, enforcement would be extremely difficult if not      
         impossible.                                                         
                                                                             
    Q  : Recently many major software companies, such as Novell and          
         Microsoft, have made a lot of noise about their software being      
         illegaly copied.  Apparently this has been going on in excess of    
         fifteen years.  What keeps the FBI from taking down all the people  
         that pirate software?                                               
                                                                             
    A  : Software piracy occurs in many forms.  One way is when a person     
         simply copies programs for another person on disk, and trades it    
         in person.  Another very common way is online.  The Internet is     
         filled with forums dedicated to computer piracy, and then there     
         are computer Bulletin Board Systems (BBSs) that are also dedicated  
         to piracy.  Restricting trade on the internet, much like with       
         child pornography, is virtually impossible because of the freedom   
         of speech and expression.  The FBI has quite a presence on the      
         Internet sites and chat channels, but can't really do much about    
         what it sees.  BBSs are slightly easier to deal with.  If the FBI   
         gathers enough incriminating information about a certain system     
         (which often takes years to achieve), it may receive a search       
         warrant to raid the operator's house.  The FBI currently has        
         access to a number of the "top" BBSs, most of which have over TEN   
         incoming phone lines.  I can not give specific information on       
         upcoming busts, but I will reveal that the FBI is working on some   
         very significant ones, and is constantly trying to end this costly  
         crime that is causing American companies huge losses.               
                                                                             
    Q  : What is the usual procedure when a person gets "busted" for         
         software piracy?                                                    
                                                                             
    A  : It's rather depressing, because the majority of the time, when we   
         catch someone pirating software, it is a person under the age of    
         eighteen.  We don't want a punishment so light that the minor will  
         disregard it and commit the crime once again, but we don't want a   
         punishment so stern that it will ruin the person's life.  When an   
         adult is caught, the outcomes can be quite serious.  Fines in the   
         hundred thousands are often imposed, and all computer equipment     
         containing illegal material is seized.  Being caught for such       
         white-collar crimes can really mess up a person's life.             
                                                                             
    Q  : What is your main hinderance from being able to take down any and   
         all BBSs that you find in violation of piracy laws?                 
                                                                             
    A  : We know about many, many boards in violation of such laws.  We can  
         even gain access to many of them, but the FBI is in sort of a       
         catch-22.  When we log on to a BBS, we often find a message         
         stating either that if we are in the FBI, we must disconnect        
         promptly, or that we must leave a message to the operator stating   
         why we want access to a board.  If, however, we do gain access to   
         a BBS, our worries are by no means over.  We have to find a file    
         containing illegal software and be able to "download" it.  Before   
         we can do this, however, we often have to send the BBS something    
         of our own.  That is where our search generally ends.  If we get    
         involved in sending a BBS some pirated software, we are in turn in  
         violation of the law.  Such activities are different from drug      
         dealing where the FBI is allowed to go undercover, and even         
         impersonate a drug dealer.  However, whenever we logon to a board   
         we are stepping into someone's house and must abide by their        
         rules.  Thus, we must have a search warrant.                        
                                                                             
    Q  : How, then, do you ever take down a BBS?                             
                                                                             
    A  : Our main resource is Narcs.  When we catch a person and impose      
         sky-high fines on them, they are usually willing to do just about   
         anything to keep from having to pay them.  This is how we find      
         the biggest of boards and stop them.                                
                                                                             
 
                                                                             
                                                                             
       Due to the fact that our interview was done by phone, the personal    
   level of contact was not there, and the FBI agent felt free to end it as  
   soon as he had to go.  Approximately 15 minutes into the interview, we    
   were forced to end it because he had a call on the other line (DOH!).     
   I think this should be a wake-up call for all of us.  It sure was for     
   us.  We often forget how vulnerable we are.  This interview clearly       
   shows what we must do to keep from getting busted, and I'm quite          
   confident that if we follow those steps, we will be alright for the next  
   few years at least.  We should keep on our toes, though, and keep up      
   with the times.  Congress is constantly debating bills that mostly        
   involve the regulation of child pornography, but could quite easily       
   effect us as well.                                                        
                                                                             
                                                                             
 ฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿฿

 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ

 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      For the past few months, the scene has been plagued by a disease      บ
 บ  called Chris Carter.  This disease would do anything to try to ruin       บ
 บ  people in the warez scene.  "Chris Carter," or so we knew him, was        บ
 บ  apparently once a warez user himself, until someone narked on his board   บ
 บ  one day, and he was forced to take it down.  Since then, he thought       บ
 บ  there might be some sort of a need for him to nark on people on the       บ
 บ  scene.  So during these months, many of us got emails from our            บ
 บ  administrators saying that they got emails from Chris Carter reporting    บ
 บ  having seen us in the action of offering pirated software on IRC, or      บ
 บ  doing various other illegal acts using the provider's system.  We all     บ
 บ  knew this Chris Carter guy by name, really having no idea who he was.     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      A few issues ago, RCN first aired the Chris Carter story in the form  บ
 บ  of a "find that nark!" contest.  It seemed humorous, like another         บ
 บ  attempt by RCN for comedy, but in reality, this was quite serious, and    บ
 บ  it would turn out to be one of the most important missions RCN has ever   บ
 บ  set out to accomplish for itself and the scene alike.  For a month now,   บ
 บ  we've been airing the "find that nark" contest, and for a month, we've    บ
 บ  received an astonishing amount of mail saying "I, too, was a victim of    บ
 บ  Chris Carter."  Some told good stories, of administrators that just put   บ
 บ  it off, others weren't so lucky.                                          บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      So let me first explain our boundaries in this.  RCN is not a cop.    บ
 บ  We have no true power in harming Chris Carter once having found him.      บ
 บ  RCN is a magazine, however, and in some ways, we will have far more       บ
 บ  power than a cop.  We have the power of words, and along with a few       บ
 บ  not-so-stupid brains, we can achieve the complete and utter destruction   บ
 บ  of Chris Carter, in minutes.  So I will first outline to you what you     บ
 บ  will find in the paragraphs to follow.  Here, you will be learning of     บ
 บ  Chris Carter's REAL name.  That's all nice and stuff, but what will you   บ
 บ  do with that to gain your revenge after a possible incidence with         บ
 บ  Chrissypooh himself?  Well, RCN is also going to provide to you his       บ
 บ  phone number so you can torment him day and night.  Then, if he's         บ
 บ  starting to piss you off, or if you're just getting bored of talking to   บ
 บ  him, we have also provided you with his parents' phone number.  All in    บ
 บ  the same house, but they have their own lines.  Finally, if Chris really  บ
 บ  got you good, and you feel that your only way of paying him back would    บ
 บ  be through a mail bomb, (no, a REAL mail bomb) RCN has provided you with  บ
 บ  his complete address, zip+4 so the bomb gets there faster.                บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Along with personal reports of incidents with Chris Carter, this      บ
 บ  past month was filled with many tips on who this person really is.  RCN   บ
 บ  followed any and all leads, calling all the numbers given to us, and the  บ
 บ  like.  But there was one thing that set the final lead off from all the   บ
 บ  others.  The last lead described a person whose name was NOT Chris        บ
 บ  Carter.  Let us for a moment put ourselves into the mind of this person.  บ
 บ  If your name were really Chris Carter, chances are you wouldn't log on    บ
 บ  and nark on people using it, right?  Furthermore, Chris Carter is quite   บ
 บ  a common name in the United States.  This tip gave us a last name,        บ
 บ  Schlegel, to work with.  It also gave us a phone number, a city, a        บ
 บ  state, and a possible workplace to deal with.  The whole lead went with   บ
 บ  all prior data that we had, such as email captures that we had received   บ
 บ  from readers, but it had the added aspect of being REALISTIC.             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      We got the lead around Thursday of this week.  On Friday night, we    บ
 บ  called the residence at the number listed, 512-282-8979, and waited for   บ
 บ  someone to pick up.  The plan, say "Hi, is Chris Carter available?" and   บ
 บ  see if he choked on his reply.  It's a good thing he didn't pick up,      บ
 บ  that plan would have gotten us nowhere.  The answering machine picked     บ
 บ  up, and we hung up.  Let me just mention the fact that we called him at   บ
 บ  about 2 am.  We called back on Saturday night, again at approximately 2   บ
 บ  am, but this time we had a better plan.  Hitex was the one to call.       บ
 บ  He's had much public speaking experience and we figured he would be the   บ
 บ  best for the job.  A man picked up.  We had a dilemma to tackle.  We      บ
 บ  didn't know his first name.  "Is Mr. Schlegel here?"  The man said that   บ
 บ  he was but it was a tad late.  I notified him that this was extremely     บ
 บ  important phone call that could result in legal consequences.  He         บ
 บ  tightened up.  He asked what it was regarding, and I notified him that    บ
 บ  it was regarding a software piracy issue that I would have to get         บ
 บ  resolved by the morning, and that I was going to be up all night working  บ
 บ  on this issue if need be.                                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      I was posing as an iD Software representative (hey can YOU come up    บ
 บ  with anything better in about 3 seconds?) working for an anti-piracy      บ
 บ  corporation and we were going to put out a major release, Quake, the      บ
 บ  following morning, and that this could involve the possible piracy of     บ
 บ  that game.  He said "Well Jim is my dad, but this is Daniel, I'm the      บ
 บ  computer guy of the house."  So apparently I was already talking to the   บ
 บ  right guy.  Obviously he got quite scared and didn't want his parents to  บ
 บ  find out about this, so he started to talk to me.  The first thing he     บ
 บ  asked me was "Does iD Software have a WWW page for this release?"         บ
 บ  Seemed like a sort of random question to ask me, but this easily showed   บ
 บ  me that this guy had Internet experience.  I gave him the address,        บ
 บ  http://www.idsoftware.com (I think).                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      I asked him if he was ever logged onto the IRC.  So the following is  บ
 บ  the information I got out of him.  He HAS been on IRC, he denied ever     บ
 บ  having stored commercial software on his account, though he had heard of  บ
 บ  several warez-related channels.  He named #fATEfiles and #Warez950.  He   บ
 บ  also named tKLP as someone he had seen before on IRC, as with g0d, and    บ
 บ  thclOne.  All people we know.  He, of course, blamed anything that would  บ
 บ  be stored on his account, if warez-related, on an evil friend that has    บ
 บ  his password.  I didn't buy it.  He said that his friend is a master      บ
 บ  hacker and everything was being done by him.  He also told me he was a    บ
 บ  beginner at the Internet.  Still, he could quite easily explain commands  บ
 บ  such as /whois on IRC.  Later, I asked him how long he had been on the    บ
 บ  Internet, and he said 6 months.  I suspect it's probably been more than   บ
 บ  that but I wasn't in a mood to argue.                                     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      I often scared him by telling him that we found out about him         บ
 บ  through traces on his Internet account, and that would lead him to        บ
 บ  spilling more information.  I ran old RCN issues and opened up NFO files  บ
 บ  and ran down the lists pointing out random names.  "Have you ever heard   บ
 บ  of <nickname>?"  He quickly answered no to all names.  Then came the      บ
 บ  kicker.  "Have you ever heard of Chris Carter?"  He choked on me.  He     บ
 บ  laughed for a bit, sounded like he was starting to cry, and then said     บ
 บ  "Golly gee, heh, they pick the darndest of names don't they?"  He lost    บ
 บ  it.                                                                       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      I continued the conversation, putting that a bit behind him.  I got   บ
 บ  a phone book and flew through it for a good name.  Then came the next     บ
 บ  kicker.  I told him that the reason we called him was actually not to     บ
 บ  charge him of any crime.  I told him we had a team of about 35 narks and  บ
 บ  that all used to be in the scene.  I told him that one of them, Greg      บ
 บ  Sneyder (I found that in the phone book ;-) decided not to stay           บ
 บ  anonymous and he is currently earning a salary helping us on our mission  บ
 บ  to stop software piracy.  I was sweetening the pot.  I told him that      บ
 บ  Chris Carter was a name we had associated with him through emails, and    บ
 บ  he tried to pass it off.  I explained to him some more money              บ
 บ  opportunities for narking.  All I wanted was to make sure he really was   บ
 บ  this Chris Carter guy.  Then, after a few minutes, I proposed once more,  บ
 บ  "I'll give you another opportunity to answer this question.  Are you      บ
 บ  Chris Carter, or do you know that person?"  He thought for a VERY long    บ
 บ  while, said "Well, ...."  or "Hmm...." and after no less than about 10    บ
 บ  seconds of pondering, he responded "No, I am not."  Now I was thoroughly  บ
 บ  convinced.                                                                บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      I spoke with him for a while longer, the whole conversation lasted a  บ
 บ  good 45 minutes.  At the end of our talk, he told me he was 14.           บ
 บ  Sounding like any good law official would, I said "Just 14?  You know,    บ
 บ  you shouldn't get yourself into these kinds of messes at that age.  You   บ
 บ  should be out playing with your friends.  These are felonious crimes,     บ
 บ  nothing a 14 year old should be messing with."  During the course of our  บ
 บ  conversation, he himself had mentioned having known Dr. Jekyll.  I don't  บ
 บ  know if it was Chris Carter (or rather Daniel Schlegel) that got Dr.      บ
 บ  Jekyll busted, but he spoke about him nonetheless, which I found          บ
 บ  extremely suspicious.  At the end of our conversation, I said "Well he    บ
 บ  was busted a bit ago, and he's over 18, so he can be tried to the full    บ
 บ  extent of the law, but he's in deep now, and though if prosecuted you     บ
 บ  wouldn't be due to your age, that does not lower its extremeness."        บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Then came the final slip-up.  Spoken like a good Texan, he said, at   บ
 บ  the conclusion of our conversation, "You you you -- you know what?        บ
 บ  I-i-i-i'm I'm a shakin' in maw boots!!"  "But why?" he must have assumed  บ
 บ  I was thinking, because after all he had denied all criminal activity.    บ
 บ  So he tried to regain his stance after choking.  "I-i-i really don't      บ
 บ  even know why, cuz I ain't done nothin' bad, but I'm still just a         บ
 บ  shakin' in maw boots!"  Now it was for sure.                              บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      So let's recap.  This guy choked every single time I mentioned Chris  บ
 บ  Carter, and once even pondered a possible money opportunity for over 10   บ
 บ  seconds when approached with this name.  Next, he seemed to be quite      บ
 บ  involved in the warez scene, denying many happenings on his account       บ
 บ  without me ever mentioning them.  And finally, he knew a whole lot about  บ
 บ  running traces on people, and about figuring out things about people on   บ
 บ  IRC.  He knew about /whois, and about how an email address is not         บ
 บ  necessarily the address found on IRC because that contains server         บ
 บ  information.  Well and sure, you would need to know that to nark on       บ
 บ  anybody from IRC because he emails the administrators of all the          บ
 บ  servers.                                                                  บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      I have never been so sure about anything as I am about this, I was    บ
 บ  an extreme skeptic going into the conversation, and an extreme skeptic    บ
 บ  coming out of the conversation.  However, all the while I was writing     บ
 บ  anything he said that might be of use later down, and I came up with an   บ
 บ  awful big list.  So we have found Chris Carter.  Now I need to clarify a  บ
 บ  bit about how we got all the information I'm about to present you with.   บ
 บ  The original phone number, 512-282-8979, the last name (Schlegel), the    บ
 บ  City, and the state were all in the original anonymous tip.  Upon         บ
 บ  calling him, I found out the following.  His dad's name is Jim and his    บ
 บ  parents' line is 512-282-2524.  This I found out because at first he      บ
 บ  assumed I wanted to talk to his parents.  His name is Daniel.  I figured  บ
 บ  that out by doing a finger on his current Internet account.  Also, that   บ
 บ  is the name on his answering machine, and the name he presented himself   บ
 บ  by.                                                                       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Does he work at Symantec?  That was also a part of the original       บ
 บ  lead.  I know why, too.  One of Daniel's many Internet accounts was one   บ
 บ  on Symantec.  However, I do believe that this was either a hacked         บ
 บ  account or that his dad works for Symantec and he was using his account.  บ
 บ  Furthermore, the Symantec concept led to another reason why this is him.  บ
 บ  He IS in the scene, that's obvious.  But how many experienced computer    บ
 บ  users, which he admitted to being, have never heard of Symantec?  When I  บ
 บ  told him that I had a lead telling me he was either working for Symantec  บ
 บ  or was using a Symantec account, he jumped and became all figity and      บ
 บ  said "WHAT?! Huh!? I ain't never heard of Symantec!"  He's definitely     บ
 บ  used their Internet account at one point or another, but I don't believe  บ
 บ  he works there.  After all, he's 14.                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Daniel's current Internet account is one being used on a CCSI         บ
 บ  computer.  CCSI stands for Commuter Communications System Incorporated,   บ
 บ  and is ccsi.com on the Internet.  His account there is mumra, so his      บ
 บ  final email address is mumra@ccsi.com.  This is further validated by the  บ
 บ  name it is made out to, Daniel Schlegel.  The rest of the information I   บ
 บ  am about to provide you with, that being his address, was generated       บ
 บ  solely as a result of his stupidity and my intuition ;-).  You will all   บ
 บ  find a very useful server on the WWW.  It's called Switchboard.  It       บ
 บ  contains every listed number in Northern America and the most amazing     บ
 บ  database searcher I have ever seen.  You can search through 90,000,000    บ
 บ  numbers in under 3 seconds.  I went in and searched for Schlegel in       บ
 บ  Austin, Texas.  I didn't expect his line to be listed, but maybe his      บ
 บ  parents' line would.  Surely enough, there was a listing, under James     บ
 บ  Schlegel (Jim is short for James).  11314 Aloysia Dr. Austin, TX          บ
 บ  78748-1846.  Note that Daniel also notified me of a second Internet       บ
 บ  account of his, on the server reallink.com.  It's amazing what a few      บ
 บ  intimidating words can do.                                                บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      The RCN staff would like to thank the anonymous tip we got on Daniel  บ
 บ  Schlegel.  You have done a great favor to the scene.  We would also like  บ
 บ  to thank each and every tip we got beforehand of letters sent to          บ
 บ  administrators.  These proved invaluable in tracing a route to this       บ
 บ  person out of older email addresses.                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      So I look back in hindsight, a tad of retrospect, and I see how well  บ
 บ  this whole ordeal really does piece together.  Each and every time we     บ
 บ  got a copy of an email this guy sent, it was from Daniel Schlegel's       บ
 บ  area.  Every single lead just pieced together.  Again, many thanks to     บ
 บ  all that participated in the "find that nark" contest, I'm sure this guy  บ
 บ  is going to be getting many many phone calls from people in the scene     บ
 บ  reading this article.  I have no doubts in my mind that he will be        บ
 บ  getting just as much torment and hell in the next few weeks as he gave    บ
 บ  some of the participants in the scene in past months.                     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 วฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤถ

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ    Author  : Hitex                                                         บ
 บ    Subject : ROR Dead!?                                                    บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ
 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Earlier this week, word was flying around IRC saying "ROR is dead!"   บ
 บ  or "ROR has retired!"  When the word made it to channel #RCN, everyone    บ
 บ  danced to the sight of 5 reporters jumping on the story.  Apparently      บ
 บ  Manic had come on stating that ROR (Release on Rampage) was retiring      บ
 บ  from the scene due to its inability to release working and usable         บ
 บ  software.  Many gasped at the news, many were finally relieved, but not   บ
 บ  I.  I became inquisitive.  Something told me that there was more to it    บ
 บ  than just a departure from the scene.                                     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      I quickly got into channel #ROR to find a [-MANiC-] in the channel.   บ
 บ  Suspecting deception, I ran a /whois on him.  Surely, it wasn't the same  บ
 บ  Manic I had known.  Perhaps he had changed his account since then?  I     บ
 บ  proceeded to run a /whois on several other ROR "members" just to find     บ
 บ  that none of their addresses matched.  I was beginning to suspect a       บ
 บ  takeover.  I asked if that was indeed what it was, and quite publically,  บ
 บ  a few people said "Yes, that's what it is."  "So ROR is still alive?"     บ
 บ  "Yes."  Oh.  Okay.  Now I had to figure out who took it over, and why!    บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      I saw a few ops in channel #ROR that I didn't recognize as ROR        บ
 บ  members.  Moreover, I DID recall them to be GODS members.  I              บ
 บ  double-checked the NFOs and surely enough, every op in the channel        บ
 บ  belonged to GODS.  I asked why GODS would be interested in taking over a  บ
 บ  small group such as ROR's channel.  I would have thought that a courier   บ
 บ  group would try to keep good relations with its release groups, but       บ
 บ  apparently I was wrong.  I also thought to myself "Well isn't this        บ
 บ  ironic?  A top courier group engaging itself into the immature act of     บ
 บ  channel takeovers? WHY!?"  Could this be an indicator of the values of    บ
 บ  GODS?  I continued to enquire, and found out that apparently ROR was      บ
 บ  messing with GODS' bots, perhaps through IP spoofing, perhaps just        บ
 บ  through idents, and that this was GODS' payback opportunity.  The         บ
 บ  following is a log of what happened in #ROR :                             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 วฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤถ
 บ                                                                            บ

 วฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤถ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Still, I was not impressed.  Out of my conversation, though, a        บ
 บ  person by the name of Starwave came out.  Allegedly, Starwave actually    บ
 บ  NARKED on tKLP saying that tKLP's girlfriend, Boost on IRC, gave him      บ
 บ  tKLP's address and phone number so he would nark on him.  Starwave        บ
 บ  autoposted tKLP's address on various public warez channels as the         บ
 บ  following log shows :                                                     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 วฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤถ

 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  <Starwave> tKLP lives at 77 Skyline Dr., Front Royal, VA 22630-5716.      บ
 บ             His phone number is (540) 636-6492.  His mother's name is      บ

 วฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤถ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Later, an interview conducted by Rebel Chicken with tKLP reveals      บ
 บ  that the address and phone number were not real.  Well, at least that's   บ
 บ  what TKLP says.  We'll show you why that might not be so true.            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      So is ROR going through a downfall?  Do they have to resort to lame   บ
 บ  bot manipulation to get anywhere?  Some might say ROR was already down,   บ
 บ  so it doesn't really matter.  Some might argue that ROR is doing better   บ
 บ  than most groups and doesn't have to resort to such things.  I'll take    บ
 บ  my own position.  ROR is definitely better than most groups, but it is    บ
 บ  BECAUSE of that, that they shouldn't have to resort to lame bot           บ
 บ  tampering to get their way.  Especially in the position of ROR, with the  บ
 บ  immature reputation that ROR possesses, I think they need to concentrate  บ
 บ  a bit more on keeping their sophistication up.  Your reputation does not  บ
 บ  result solely from your releases, and ROR can't boast in that area        บ
 บ  either.                                                                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      With as much confusion as and shit that ROR is going through, I       บ
 บ  don't think they're in any position to boast much, regardless of their    บ
 บ  releases.  But then, I don't think GODS is in much of a position to be    บ
 บ  taking channels either.                                                   บ

 บ  by manipulating the exe filedates.                                        บ

 บ        everyone owning a modem is a secondary issue.                       บ

 บ        people believe that to be the best, you have to release the most,   บ
 บ        or the best games.  This is not necessarily the case.  To be the    บ
 บ        best group, you must be respected, and feared, by those capable of  บ
 บ        competing with you.  Only when other respectable cracking groups    บ
 บ        recognize that you consistently beat them are you the best.  Some   บ
 บ        groups try to get around this harsh reality by releasing a lot.     บ

 บ        groups, a powerful desire to crush the opposition in every way      บ
 บ        possible.  Those who pretend to be releasing only for the masses    บ
 บ        will never be happy unless they admit to themselves that they are   บ
 บ        in it to win it                                                     บ

 บ        best, not necessarily acknowledge that you are the best.  Often,    บ

 บ        the truth in order to admit it to yourself.  Also, the Ware Report  บ

 บ        Razor 1911's never made any mistakes.                               บ

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ    Author  : g0d                                                           บ
 บ    Subject : fATE Vice President Disses fATE                               บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ
 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      And then there was none.  Well guys, that's it.  I'm done.  I have    บ
 บ  committed the ultimate crime against warez-heads everywhere.  That's      บ
 บ  right, I have gone and gotten a life.  It's been a fun bunch-o-years      บ
 บ  kickin' it on the net with you guys, but now I think it's time I packed   บ
 บ  it in, I have been semi-successfully running a real life computer         บ
 บ  business, and trying to run groups and such on the Internet.  Now I       บ
 บ  think the time has come to drop the scene and take my "quickly growing"   บ
 บ  I might add computer business to the top.                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      So, my personal opinion of the scene.  I have been around quite a     บ
 บ  while now, I think most people in most groups either know me personally   บ
 บ  or at least know of me, and I think owe the time I have spent bouncing    บ
 บ  warez to the four corners of the globe that I have acquired a pretty      บ
 บ  good feel for the scene and how it works.                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      I see people every day saying how the scene is dead or dying, etc.    บ
 บ  And you know what?  I agree.  It's just not fun any more.  Too many       บ
 บ  damned AOL lamers and dick heads coming out of nowhere.  Every day I get  บ
 บ  messaged at least a dozen times by some lamer looking for "elite warez"   บ
 บ  or some shit.  I mean, pack the whole scene up, open a private            บ
 บ  warez-head only IRC server and go there, because the Effnet is infested   บ
 บ  with lameness.  There are still a few elite people left but only a FEW.   บ
 บ  The rest are for the most part a large combination of 50% lamers, 20%     บ
 บ  feds, 25% Microsoft undercover lamer/feds, and on a good day, 5% future   บ
 บ  elite people.                                                             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      As far as groups go, I would have to say that the best died with      บ
 บ  good old TDU-JAM! as far as games go.  Razor 1911 is eternal.  I see      บ
 บ  Prestige is kicking major ass.  However, they are packed full of          บ
 บ  big-ass-egos and I can't see them surviving longer than a few more        บ
 บ  months.  ROR has good old tKLP still tromping around, Hybrid was once a   บ
 บ  big name and is now barely alive, and then there are a bunch of lesser    บ
 บ  lame little games groups.                                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      As for apps, DOD (Drink or Die) was once king of the hill, but now I  บ
 บ  can't really give anyone props.  It seems the whole scene is either       บ
 บ  getting busted, been busted, or just in a major slump.  As for courier    บ
 บ  groups, Amnesia is doing pretty well, RiSC has been the same for as long  บ
 บ  as I can remember, simply the best, MALiCE has pretty much died and so    บ
 บ  has RTS.  Then there are a gaggle of other little groups trying to get    บ
 บ  by.  Man, thinking about this makes me sick.  There are only 2 REAL       บ
 บ  groups left.  Razor 1911 and RiSC.  All the others are pretty much        บ
 บ  barely staying together with daily political/ego battles where the group  บ
 บ  is constantly in a state of fluxx.  You know, sorta like fATE (Fast       บ
 บ  Action Trade Exchange)!                                                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Now everyone is asking me to say my piece about fATE.  Well here it   บ
 บ  is.  Finally my honest feelings about fATE.  Well, Anti Derivative has    บ
 บ  been President since the day I assisted him in taking over the group      บ
 บ  from Red Dog.  Anti Derivative is a pretty decent guy in person and is    บ
 บ  fairly good at fixing the constant arguments going on in fATE.            บ
 บ  Otherwise (and sorry Anti Derivative if you're reading this) he is not    บ
 บ  really efficient at running a group.  He really doesn't do anything       บ
 บ  other than just break up arguments by kicking people out, and I think he  บ
 บ  just sticks around because he likes the power trip of being able to log   บ
 บ  on and boss people around and be the leader for a while.  Anyone who      บ
 บ  dares say he isn't doing a good job immediately gets kicked out of fATE   บ
 บ  and that's that.  I think fATE would benefit from a change of command.    บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      I tried when I was a member to make changes but Anti Derivative       บ
 บ  would just change them back the same old un-working ways of the old       บ
 บ  fATE.  Doobie, the Vice President, I hate his guts and would love to      บ
 บ  string him up and skin him alive.  The guy has no clue.  Period.          บ
 บ  Therefore my final feelings on fATE are, there are still a couple of      บ
 บ  good guys left in there to chat.  I would pretty much say that fATE is    บ
 บ  the equivalent of #NTA-Nokturnal.  Basically a dead group who used to     บ
 บ  have a big name.                                                          บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Just hanging out in a channel and "unlike" #NTA-Nokturnal where       บ
 บ  everything is fun and smooth, they basically sit in #fATE and argue and   บ
 บ  bitch and moan and say how great they are etc.  Not really my cup of tea  บ
 บ  any more.  So there ya go, in a nut shell, I say fATE is pretty much      บ
 บ  dead.  If it were to be reviewed it would have to be under new            บ
 บ  leadership and would need a miracle.  Well I guess I have said my piece,  บ
 บ  I gotta jet, got REAL LIFE WORK to do!  Yippeee, I finally got a life!    บ
 บ                                                                            บ

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ    Author  : Garf                                                          บ
 บ    Subject : The Death of Bulletin Board Systems                           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ
 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      The BBS scene has drastically changed due to the Internet and         บ
 บ  everything it has brought.  If you think about it, just last year BBSes   บ
 บ  were far more popular than IRC (Internet Relay Chat).  Lately, however,   บ
 บ  BBSes have been at a sharp downfall and at this rate, they will become    บ
 บ  extinct in the near future.  So why is this happening?                    บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Before the popularity of the Internet, BBSes were the only method of  บ
 บ  file transfer, and the only way to pick up the latest scene news.  All    บ
 บ  the way back in 1990, the 2400 baud modem was still the standard.         บ
 บ  Boards were not nearly what they are now.  At 2400, ANSI was kept to a    บ
 บ  minimum, extremely small files were transfered, and BBS software was not  บ
 บ  very advanced at all.  As the years went on, faster modems brought more   บ
 บ  ANSI and greater size in transfers.  With the advent of the 14.4, the     บ
 บ  warez scene was brought to its peak.  The size of the warez was a lot     บ
 บ  smaller in relation to the speed of the modem, and files were moved       บ
 บ  quickly between the various BBSes.  However, the advent of the 28.8       บ
 บ  brought radically different results.  Warez became much larger and the    บ
 บ  speed of the modems just couldn't keep up with that of the size of        บ
 บ  warez.  The frustratingly slow speed of file transfers led to the         บ
 บ  resulting usage of the Internet as a form of data distribution.  No       บ
 บ  longer would warez traders have to transfer files at a mere 3 kb/s.       บ
 บ  They could now enjoy speeds nearing 500 kb/s.  Obviously, a huge          บ
 บ  advantage.                                                                บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Still, a BBS has something that the Internet dos not.  If you have    บ
 บ  ever been the System Operator of a BBS, you know what I'm talking about.  บ
 บ  A BBS is a form of interconnectivity where everybody knows each other.    บ
 บ  It is a place where people become good friends and after a prolonged      บ
 บ  period of time, become long-time users.  Message bases are also           บ
 บ  interesting advantages of a BBS and are very distinct from IRC or         บ
 บ  Internet Newsgroups.  Posting questions on a BBS message base guarantees  บ
 บ  a reliable answer from someone you know and trust, where posting on a     บ
 บ  newsgroup isn't as personal because you don't know anybody that you're    บ
 บ  talking to, or their credibility.  Door games, of course, were another    บ
 บ  great attraction of a BBS, and Internet MUDs can hardly be compared to    บ
 บ  them.  The Internet has fully taken over.  It has begun to make its       บ
 บ  kill.                                                                     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      I have been a SysOp for 14 months now.  When I first put it up,       บ
 บ  BBSes were prospering and doing quite well.  Lately, it has become a      บ
 บ  struggle to gain new users and raise adequate activity.  I remember when  บ
 บ  there were about 50 good boards in any given area.  Now, it is hard to    บ
 บ  name 5.  Every SysOp has become sick and tired of the crap that has       บ
 บ  taken the BBS scene down.  If everyone gives up, the whole scene will     บ
 บ  die.  I've pondered taking down my BBS, but then I ask myself, "What      บ
 บ  else would my computer be doing during the day?" And of course, the       บ
 บ  answer is nothing.  Why should I take down a BBS that is doing fairly     บ
 บ  well and is promoting the scene?  I won't.  But I hope others will do     บ
 บ  the same as I.                                                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      The best way, given the proper resources, to setup a good BBS is to   บ
 บ  provide it with telnet connectivity.  There are still very few telnet     บ
 บ  BBSes out there, probably due to the fact that it isn't exactly an easy   บ
 บ  task to setup, but for those of us who can, I would encourage it.  It's   บ
 บ  obvious that the Internet isn't going to magically disappear and give     บ
 บ  the BBS scene a second chance, but should we really want it to?  Why not  บ
 บ  take advantage of this newfound resource?  The number of FTP Sites is     บ
 บ  growing faster than that of BBSes going down.  Along with it, every site  บ
 บ  that is brought up could, with some work, be converted into a telnet      บ
 บ  BBS.  That of course would mean that we could continue having all the     บ
 บ  things we once loved about BBSes, but at faster speeds.  So be it         บ
 บ  regular dial-in boards, or full-time telnet BBSes, we should encourage    บ
 บ  the revival of boards.  They are the key to keeping the scene alive.      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ    Author  : Waynekerr                                                     บ
 บ    Subject : Quick FTP Advice                                              บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ
 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      The Internet warez scene has brought about several new innovations.   บ
 บ  Along with it, come a new form of data transfer, FTP sites.  This is a    บ
 บ  skill that all newbie warez dudes are going to have to master right away  บ
 บ  so they can excel in the scene.  If you're not on FTP sites, it means     บ
 บ  you have no warez.  What does that mean?  That means that your only form  บ
 บ  of copying files is through DCC.  That's not good.  But fear not, Uncle   บ
 บ  Wayne is here to explain it to all of you lesser mortals.                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      The most popular type of site is, of course, the anonymous site.      บ
 บ  You know, the ones that you hear about, then die 2.5 hours later.         บ
 บ  Setting one up couldn't be easier.  What you look for is a writeable      บ
 บ  directory :                                                               บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  drwxrwxr-x   8 ftp   anon     1024 Mar 17 02.26 .                         บ
 บ  drwxrwxr-x   8 ftp   anon     1024 Mar 17 02.26 ..                        บ
 บ  drwxrwxr-x   8 ftp   anon     1024 Mar 17 02.26 bin                       บ
 บ  drwxrwxr-x   8 ftp   anon     1024 Mar 17 02.26 etc                       บ
 บ  drwxrwxrwx   8 ftp   anon     1024 Jun 21 04.22 incoming <-- HERE!        บ
 บ  drwxrwxr-x   8 ftp   anon     1024 Mar 17 02.26 pub                       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      As you can see, the /incoming directory is 'world-writeable.'  That   บ
 บ  means you can write files there, and therefore create directories.        บ
 บ  Happy happy.  But first you need to check that directories created        บ
 บ  within the /incoming directory can be written to.  Many FTP daemons by    บ
 บ  default create all directories (especially those created by 'anon'        บ
 บ  users) with drwxrwxr-x permissions, i.e. you get no joy from them, so be  บ
 บ  sure to check this before yu can think about transfering 60 gigs of       บ
 บ  warez.  If however you CAN write to your newly created directory, you     บ
 บ  are in luck.  Another point worthy of note here is that you might be      บ
 บ  able to use the 'chmod' command to change permissions on a directory      บ
 บ  you've created.                                                           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      So if you make a directory called /incoming/.gamez (how original)     บ
 บ  and it gets created without write permissions for you, try 'chmod 777     บ
 บ  .games' to make it drwxrwxrwx (world-writeable).  That's pretty much it!  บ
 บ  Try and use your common sense, don't create dirs called '.gamez,'         บ
 บ  '.warez,' etc. because these will only get raped by people using          บ
 บ  ftpsearch and the like.                                                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Directories with names including control characters are a popular     บ
 บ  method of hiding the location of your warez-stash, using ^H (delete) is   บ
 บ  a good one as many ftp clients write the delete char as raw and it        บ
 บ  deletes the character before, so a directory called 'games^H^H^H^H^H'     บ
 บ  shows up as ''.  This is however far from foolproof, read the man pages   บ
 บ  for FTP next time you're (ab)using your shell accounts; ls -alb will      บ
 บ  give you the ascii codes for the control characters in a directory, so    บ
 บ  "..." shows up something like "015\015\015" (I'm not saying 015 is the    บ
 บ  correct ctrl character, I'm merely illustrating how it works).            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Be VERY aware, however, before you do any of this that what you are   บ
 บ  doing is 100% for sure logged, on a unix system in /var/admn/xferlog or   บ
 บ  something similar :                                                       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  Tue Jun 11 03:30:25 1996 1 0day.warez.com 685                             บ
 บ  /incoming/.warez/quake1.zip                                               บ
 บ  b _ o r warezuser ftp 0 *                                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      This is bad news for you if the admin checks his/her logs with any    บ
 บ  kind of regularity - as you can see they have the time you connected,     บ
 บ  the host you connected from, the username, etc.  So you can be sure if    บ
 บ  you're not using a hacked account that you're going to get your wrists    บ
 บ  slapped.  But you'd never be THAT stupid, right?!                         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Another thing I feel I should mention is, watch how you access the    บ
 บ  net.  If you think using a hacked shell on iam.verylame.edu by            บ
 บ  telnetting from your carded netcom account is safe, please think again.   บ
 บ  Most sites, EVEN .edu's are now hip to the warez scene, basically due to  บ
 บ  all the trouble we've caused, along with the H/P types, TCPWRAPPERS,      บ
 บ  which log detailed information on every connection in/out of machines     บ
 บ  are very popular nowadays, and any administrator with a clue can          บ
 บ  recreate your session using publically available utilities telling        บ
 บ  him/her exacly what you typed while you were online, etc.  So BEWARE!     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Stay safe, and remember, the more steps you put between yourself and  บ
 บ  the 'target' site, the more trouble it is to catch you - it might take    บ
 บ  you an hour longer to get that 20 disk release to your home machine, but  บ
 บ  it's vastly preferable to sharing a cell with Bubba, the 7 foot guy who   บ
 บ  wants you to be his 'friend' for the night.                               บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ

 ฐ ฐฐ ฐ ฿฿ฐ ฐ฿ ฿฿ ฐ  ฿฿฿฿฿฿฿ ฐ  ฐฐฐฐฐฐ ฐฐฐ
        ฿        ฐ฿฿฿฿฿฿   ฿฿       ฿฿

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ    Author  : Genocide                                                      บ
 บ    Subject : Bigger Files = The Real Need For Speed?  The Future Awaits... บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ
 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      With files rising in meggage at a exponential rate, will new          บ
 บ  technology help the scene survive?  According to new advancements in      บ
 บ  modems, and telecommunications, the answer is a positive yes.  With       บ
 บ  ISDN, ADSL, Cable Modeming, and Satellite connections, the scene will     บ
 บ  not only survive, but will flourish as the 21st century approaches.       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Although many people like to refer to ISDN as (I.t S.till D.oes       บ
 บ  N.othing), the correct term is (Integrated Services Digital Network).     บ
 บ  Currently, ISDN is a pipe dream to many, and a fountain of youth (and     บ
 บ  speed) to few.  However, the future is bright for this prodigy of the     บ
 บ  telecommunications backbone.  Many ISPs, and even Online Services are     บ
 บ  beginning to offer ISDN as an option when you signup, etc.  With bigger   บ
 บ  files, and new CD-Rom technologies such as the DVD-Rom which allows as    บ
 บ  much as 10 gigs of information on one disc, coming out, the need for a    บ
 บ  better modem and phone line will be inevitable for even the smallest      บ
 บ  pirates.  Thus, at almost 128k baud, ISDN is one of the most              บ
 บ  cost-efficient, and communicable services available nationwide. In the    บ
 บ  near future, ISDN (along with Cable Modems, and ADSL) will be the         บ
 บ  standard in telecommunications.                                           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      With higher transfer rates than even the fastest analog modems, ISDN  บ
 บ  will help pirates transfer those big files in a snap.  Combined with its  บ
 บ  speed, superior choice between ISPs, limited hardware requirements, and   บ
 บ  availability, ISDN is the best choice for local boards, pirates, and      บ
 บ  even FTP site-ops until better technology pushes ISDN out of the way.     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      ADSL, a faster option to ISDN in some cases, is another alternative   บ
 บ  that will surely be a topic of conversation in the future of the scene.   บ
 บ  ADSL is fast enough for downloading, yet its uploading rates are still    บ
 บ  questionable at only 64 kb/s.  While it can transfer 1 meg in less than   บ
 บ  10 seconds, or as much as 6 megs in 10 seconds, it can only upload at a   บ
 บ  rate of 384 kb/s per minute, which is not as fast as ISDN.  Another       บ
 บ  disadvantage of ADSL is the fact that it is a very inefficient way of     บ
 บ  dialing out, due to its cost inefficiency (300-500 installation + by the  บ
 บ  minute calls).  Although not as cost efficient as ISDN, ADSL is a faster  บ
 บ  downloading alternative for the leechers in the scene.  However, in my    บ
 บ  humble opinion, ADSL is not as good as ISDN because of its limited        บ
 บ  availability, lack of choice in ISP, and high tariff rates when dialing   บ
 บ  out.                                                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      With the Cable Modem, a person can literally transfer a whole day's   บ
 บ  worth of trading (1 gig or so), onto their Hard drive in a few minutes.   บ
 บ  Downloading at 10 megs per second, this monster can download around 60    บ
 บ  megs per minute.  The Cable modem runs off of coaxial cable (your         บ
 บ  existing cable lines), and will run through a 10Base-T Connection, and    บ
 บ  then through the modem.  After checking a current price range at my       บ
 บ  local cable company, it is offerred in the range of (300-500              บ
 บ  installation + $30 month), which is incredible considering the amount of  บ
 บ  money that will be saved in phone bills, etc.  For the few that are       บ
 บ  fortunate to have one of these, you know what I am talking about.  The    บ
 บ  only minor disadvantages for the cable modem are its lack of              บ
 บ  availability, and limited choice of ISP until this monster spreads out.   บ
 บ  However, this is the best for its cost efficiency, and download/upload    บ
 บ  times are the fastest of all.                                             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      The final option in future telecommunications is the satellite        บ
 บ  receiver.  If a person has an existing satellite for their TV, then this  บ
 บ  might be the best option, considering its lack of hardware installation.  บ
 บ  All a person needs is a minor satellite receiver (hooks onto an           บ
 บ  expansion port, or in some cases, an infrared port), and the satellite    บ
 บ  broadcaster.  Although it may be cost effective, and easy installation    บ
 บ  for anyone who has an existing satellite, this monster will not be a      บ
 บ  major improvement, and in some cases it will be slower than some analog   บ
 บ  modems with its slow upload rate at only 28.8 kb/s.  However, satellite   บ
 บ  communications does have its advantages.  One, being that it is cost      บ
 บ  effective ($16-$40 per month, PC Magazine Figures {June 11, 1996, Vol.    บ
 บ  15 No. 11}) and no installation charges if an existing satellite is       บ
 บ  already connected with a major service.  Another advantage of satellite   บ
 บ  communications is, "It is expected to be on the fast-ramp up, following   บ
 บ  this coming year" (PC Magazine, pg. 144).  On another downnote however,   บ
 บ  the satellite communications option will limit the user to no choice in   บ
 บ  ISP until the end of next year (September 1997).                          บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Over the next few years, the scene will see a major change.  Bigger   บ
 บ  file sizes will either cause existing pirates to check out, and leave     บ
 บ  the scene due to price constraints, or to thrive in a better scene with   บ
 บ  faster warez.  As this dilemna occurs in everyone's life, this writer     บ
 บ  personally hopes that a majority of you decide to stay on.  At the end    บ
 บ  of this tunnel, there will be a better tomorrow.  In the end though,      บ
 บ  ISDN appears to reign supreme, at least for a year or so.                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  "I'd rather be optimistic, and be a fool, then be a pessimist, and be     บ
 บ  right." - Unknown                                                         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ

 บ    Author  : Rebel Chicken                                                 บ
 บ    Subject : Group Reviews : Games                                         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Hello, and welcome to Reality Check Network's all new group review!   บ
 บ  Here I will be reviewing the 5 best games release groups in the scene.    บ
 บ  Well, actually, *I* won't be the one reviewing them, *THEY* will be!      บ
 บ  It's all up to the groups, this is where quantity DOES count, but you     บ
 บ  will soon enough find that quality by far outweighs quantity.  Let's      บ
 บ  review the criteria I'll be using for judging releases.  The following    บ
 บ  is the scoring basis I'll be using :                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  Points :                                                                  บ
 บ  --------                                                                  บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  [-3] The game didn't work and a crack/fix was not released within 72      บ
 บ       hours.  The group may regain the 3 lost points by releasing a crack  บ
 บ       or fix, even beyond the 3 day period.                                บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  [ 1] The game was a dupe or freeware,                                     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  [ 2] Unsatisfactory,                                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  [ 3] Average,                                                             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  [ 4] Above Average, and                                                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  [ 5] Excellent!                                                           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      A group may lose points the following week and have their releases    บ
 บ  labeled as broken (thus receiving the proper amout of points).  If the    บ
 บ  group has released a fix between the two issues, we'll give them credit   บ
 บ  accordingly.  If a group releases a fix within a 3 day period, the        บ
 บ  game will be rated as if it worked in the first place, thus getting the   บ
 บ  3 points it lost back and any points it would have earned.  If a group    บ
 บ  releases a fix after the 3 day period has expired, it will receive its 3  บ
 บ  points back, but get no more.  Betas may receive no more than 3 points.   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ฬออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออน
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  ฺฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฟ  บ
 บ  ณ            Dates of Games Reviewed : 05/23/96 -> 05/29/96            ณ  บ
 บ  ภฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤู  บ

 บ  Pacific Theater of Operations 2 for Win 01/04                             บ

                                         ฿     r e v i e w s !

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ    Author  : Rebel Chicken                                                 บ
 บ    Subject : Group Reviews : Games                                         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Hello, and welcome to Reality Check Network's all new group review!   บ
 บ  Here I will be reviewing the 5 best games release groups in the scene.    บ
 บ  Well, actually, *I* won't be the one reviewing them, *THEY* will be!      บ
 บ  It's all up to the groups, this is where quantity DOES count, but you     บ
 บ  will soon enough find that quality by far outweighs quantity.  Let's      บ
 บ  review the criteria I'll be using for judging releases.  The following    บ
 บ  is the scoring basis I'll be using :                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  Points :                                                                  บ
 บ  --------                                                                  บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  [-3] The game didn't work and a crack/fix was not released within 72      บ
 บ       hours.  The group may regain the 3 lost points by releasing a crack  บ
 บ       or fix, even beyond the 3 day period.                                บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  [ 1] The game was a dupe or freeware,                                     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  [ 2] Unsatisfactory,                                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  [ 3] Average,                                                             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  [ 4] Above Average, and                                                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  [ 5] Excellent!                                                           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      A group may lose points the following week and have their releases    บ
 บ  labeled as broken (thus receiving the proper amout of points).  If the    บ
 บ  group has released a fix between the two issues, we'll give them credit   บ
 บ  accordingly.  If a group releases a fix within a 3 day period, the        บ
 บ  game will be rated as if it worked in the first place, thus getting the   บ
 บ  3 points it lost back and any points it would have earned.  If a group    บ
 บ  releases a fix after the 3 day period has expired, it will receive its 3  บ
 บ  points back, but get no more.  Betas may receive no more than 3 points.   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ฬออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออน
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  ฺฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฟ  บ
 บ  ณ            Dates of Games Reviewed : 05/30/96 -> 06/05/96            ณ  บ
 บ  ภฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤู  บ
 บ                                                                            บ
